This is the fifty third issue of the Statistical Year 
Book for the year 2025. The Book is issued annually 
by National Centre for Statistics and Information in 
view of the increasing importance of the statistical 
data, Alongside gradual transformation of the 
international community to information-based 
society, and the increased reliance of decision 
makers and planners on the available statistical 
data for studying and analyzing options before 
to formulation of policies, strategies and taking 
appropriate decisions

develop the contents of the book and its presentation 
style, aiming to cover all the economic and social 
activities in order to provide all the required 
statistical data which is necessary for both the public 
and private sectors, the establishments, individuals 
and groups of researchers, scholars and others.

The Sultanate of Oman occupies the South-Eastern corner 
of the Arabian Peninsula and is located between Latitudes 
16 40 and 26 20 North and Longitudes 51 50 and 59 
40 East. It has a coastal line extending almost 3165 kms., 
from the Strait of Hormuz in the North to the borders of the 
Republic of Yemen, overlooking three seas; the Arabian 
Gulf, Oman Sea and the Arabian Sea.
. ุนูุงู ูุญุจุฑ ุงูุนุฑุจ

 ููุน ุงูููููุฉ ุงูุนุฑุจูุฉ ุงูุณุนูุฏูุฉ ุบุฑุจุง ูุฏููุฉ ุงุงููุงุฑุงุช ุงูุนุฑุจูุฉ ุงููุชุญุฏุฉ
The Sultanate is bordered to Western South by the Republic 
of Yemen and the West by the Kingdom of Saudi Arabia 
and by the UAE to the North and West.

The total area of the Sultanate of Oman is 309.5 thousand 
sq. kms., and it is the Third largest country in the Arabian 
Peninsula.

The Sultanate is composed of varying topographic areas 
consisting of plains, wadis and mountains. The most 
important area is the plain overlooking the Oman Sea and 
the Arabian Sea with an area of about 3% of the total. The 
mountain ranges occupy about 15% of the total, the most 
important of which are โAl Hajrโ, extending in the form of 
an arch from Ras Musandam in the North to Ras Al-Had 
and Al Qaraโ in the South Western corner of Oman. The 
remaining area is mainly sand and desert which includes 
part of Ar Rub Al-Khali occupying about 82% of the total 
area.

The climate differs from one area to another, it is hot and 
humid in the coastal areas in summer, hot and dry in the 
interior with the exception of higher mountains, which 
enjoy a moderate climate throughout the year. The climate 
of the Dhofar Governorate is also moderate. Generally, the 
Sultanate has little and irregular rains. though heavy rains 
fall at times with the exception of Dhofar Governorate 
where heavy and regular rains fall between June and 
October because of monsoons.

Administrative Regions :

October 2011, Sultanate of Oman is divided into eleven 
Governorates.

Muscat Governorate :
The Governorate consists of Six Wilayats : Muscat, 
Mutrah, Al Amrat, Bawshar, As Seeb and Qurayyat.

It is an old city and enjoys a strategic location. Muscat 
is full of historical monuments. The most famous are: 
Al-Jalali and Al-Mirani Forts.

The Governorate consists of the Ten Wilayats : Salalah, 
Thumrayt, Taqah, Mirbat, Sadah, Rakhyut, Dalkut, 
Muqshin, Shalim Wa Juzor Al Hallaniyat and Al Mazuna. 
This area occupies nearly one third of the Sultanateโs 
total area and is one of the very few areas in the Arabian 
Peninsula with a wide range of topographic variations. It 
includes many historical monuments and cities such as 
Sumharam Port and the graves of Prophet Ayoub and Hood. 
Its people are engaged in agriculture activities and fishing.

Bait Bahr. Buraimiโs villages are watered by 49 falajes. 
Much of the rest of the wilayat is sandy desert.

The Governorate consists of nine Wilayats : Nizwa, 
Jabal Al-Akhdhar, Bahla, Manah, Al Hamra, Adam, 
Izki, Samail and BidBid. This is a central plateau running 
from Jabel Al Akhdar in the north towards the desert in 
the South. It is bordered on the West by Adh Dhahirah 
and on the east by Ash Sharqiyah. There are four main 
Valleys; Al-Abyadh, Halfein, Bahla and Samail. Samail 
and Al-Halfein together form a natural gap in the Al-Hajar 
mountain range, providing a traditional route between 
Muscat and the Ad Dakhliyah Region.

The regional center of the Ad Dakhliyah Governorate, 
at a distance of 180 kms. from Muscat. It is famous 
for its historical features, the most important of which 
are the Nizwa Fort and the Daris Falaj, the largest Falaj 
in Oman. The Falaj provides irrigation facilities for 
cultivation of dates, lemon, mango, sugarcane and 
others.

Ar Rustaq:
Ar Rustaq is the Governorate Center of the South Part 
of Al Batinah South Governorate, and it is surrounded 
by Al Hajar Al Gharby mountain range from three 
directions and is at a distance of around 160 kms. from 
Muscat. It is famous for its historical buildings such as 
Al Hazm and Ar Rustaq Castles, besides Ain Al-Kasfa 
with its hot mineral springs and dates processing factory.

The Governorate consists of Three Wilyats : Ibri, Yanqul 
and Dank. This Governorate is a semi-desert plain sloping 
from the Southern wings of Al Hajr Al Gharby in the 
direction of Ar Rub Al-Khali. It is separated from Al 
Dakhliyah Governorate by Al Kur Mountain to the East, 
it joins the Ar Rub Al Khali from the West and Al Wusta 
Governorate from the South.

Al Wusta Governorate:
The Governorate consists of Four Wilayats : Hayma, 
Mahawt, Ad Duqm and Al Jazir. It is characterized by its 
abundant oil and fisheries resources, which constitute the 
major export commodities of the Sultanate. Fishing 
and animal husbandary are the main occupation of its 
population.

climate tables in this year compared to previous years, 
where this section presents the most important indicators 
of the climate in the Sultanate of Oman, such as average

and total rainfall by weather ground stations for each 
governorate.

This section highlights some of the most important 
indicators related to the population in Oman, by the end 
of December each year. It also addresses some of the vital 
statistics, such as birth, death, and total fertility rates.

This section presents statistics and indicators related to the 
land use in the Sultanate such as the number of planned, 
granted and first-time registered land plots, their distribution 
and the real estate transaction values by governorates and 
type of use. It also addresses the number of beneficiaries 
cases of program housing support, as well as the number 
of permits and certificates of completion of construction 
classified according to the various governorates.

This section displays the cultivated area estimates, 
production of agricultural crops in the Sultanate of Oman 
and their various distributions by type and governorate. 
It also addresses the most important livestock indicators, 
estimates of domestic production of some processed 
animal products, and the number of animals vaccinated.

This section highlights some of the fisheries indicators 
in the Sultanate of Oman, mainly the total production of 
fish according to the type of fishing and governorates. It 
highlights also fish exports by country, type, and quantity.
.ุตุงุฏุฑุงุช ุงุงููุณุงู ุญุณุจ ุงูุฏููุฉ ูููุน ููููุฉ ุงุงููุณุงู
The artisanal fishing data are collected by selecting a 
sample of landing sites within a certain number of days 
of the month. The commercial fishing data are collected 
through comprehensive counting of each ship during 
a single trip. Fish exports and imports are collected by 
counting all fish shipments in the checkpoints.

This section deals with various indicators of electricity 
and water in the Sultanate of Oman, such as electricity 
and water production, installed capacity power station, 
electric power consumed and its distribution according to 
the types of consumption, distribution of electricity and 
water production according to the different governorates, 
and the number of connections.

indicators in the Sultanate of Oman, including trade 
exchange, commodity exports and imports and the 
distribution of each by commodity group and country, and 
the balance of payments.

The commodity classification used in the foreign trade 
data is the harmonized system adopted in Sultanate of 
Oman since 1987, in addition to the SITC revision (4) 
for international comparisons. Commodity values are 
estimated in Omani Rial based on the (C.I.F) value for 
imports (i.e. the cost of transport, insurance and freight 
of goods to the custom points in Oman) and (F.O.B) for 
exports and re-exports.

This section presents indicators related to the transport 
sector in the Sultanate of Oman, notably traffic of seaports, 
airports, cargo, lengths of roads executed, total vehicle 
driving licenses issued, and the number of new vehicles 
registered.

The Sultanate of Oman applied the new system of National 
Accounts (SNA) approved by the United Nations Bureau 
of Statistics and the United Nations Economic and Social 
Council in 2008. The new system adopted 2018 as a new 
base year for (SNA) in Oman instead of 2010. In addition to 
implementing the new international standards, the National 
Center for Statistics and Information has implemented the 
International Standard Industrial Classification for all 
economic activities, the (fourth revision) and the second 
version of the classification of products.

The system has been applied in the Sultanate of Oman to 
prepare a series of national accounts for the period 2010-
2021 to calculate production accounts and calculate income 
generation according to international recommendations.

Omanโs economy recorded a growth rate of 1.4% at 
constant prices in 2023 (according to definitive estimates), 
followed by a slight acceleration in the growth rate to reach 
1.6% in 2024 (preliminary estimates). This performance 
reflects relative stability in the Omani economy compared 
to some GCC economies that were affected by oil price 
fluctuations and production cuts under the "OPEC+" 
agreements.

Oil activities recorded a slight growth of 0.1% at constant 
prices in 2023, before declining by 2.7% in 2024. This 
decline is mainly attributed to the reduction in crude 
oil production as part of Omanโs commitments under 
the โOPEC+โ agreements. The average daily crude oil 
production decreased by 5.3%, reaching 992.6 thousand 
barrels per day in 2024, compared to 1,048.7 thousand 
barrels per day in 2023. In contrast, natural gas production 
increased by 4.8%, with Omanโs total production of 
natural gas (both associated and non-associated gas) 
reaching approximately 56.5 million cubic meters in 2024, 
compared to 53.9 million cubic meters in 2023.

Non-oil activities recorded a growth rate of 2.3% in 2023, 
with an acceleration to 3.5% in 2024. This development 
reflects improved performance across several industrial 
and service activities that form the base of economic 
diversification in the Sultanate of Oman. In 2024, growth 
was primarily driven by the exceptional performance of 
manufacturing activities, particularly the refined petroleum 
products industry, which recorded strong growth of 52.7% 
compared to 11.6% in 2023. Additionally, the chemical 
industries rebounded from a contraction of 1.5% in 2023 
to achieve 6.0% growth in 2024. Other manufacturing 
industries also grew by 3.9% after shrinking by 3.7% 
in 2023. In the services sector, the transport and storage 
sector โ considered a relatively significant activity โ 
contributed notably to non-oil growth, rising by 4.0% in 
2024 compared to 2.8% in 2023. The electricity and water 
supply activity also achieved growth of 6.6% in 2024. 
Despite a decline in the hotels and restaurants activity by 
3.3% in 2024 after a 6.0% increase in 2023, the rest of 
the service sectors maintained relative stability, such as the 
telecommunications and information services activities, 
which grew by 1.7%. In agriculture, the activity recorded a 
growth rate of 3.7%, while the fishing continued its strong 
performance, achieving 11.8% growth in 2024, up from 
4.0% in 2023.

2023 ุชุทูุฑ ูุชูุงูุช ูู ููููุงุช ุงูุทูุจ ุงูููุงุฆู ุฎุงูู ุนุงูู-
- Divergent trends in final demand components during 
2023 and 2024
2024ู
In terms of final demand, merchandise and services 
exports at constant prices recorded a growth of 9.1% in 
2024, compared to an increase of 2.9% in 2023. In contrast, 
imports rose by 9.7% in 2024, up from 2.0% in 2023. As 
a result, the growth rate of net external trade in goods and 
services reached 7.7% in 2024, after standing at 4.9% in 
2023. On the other hand, gross fixed capital formation 
increased by 7.1% in 2024, showing an acceleration 
compared to the 2.4% growth recorded in 2023. Final 
consumption grew by 3.2% in 2024, compared to 5.0% 
in 2023.

This section reviews banking statistics and their various 
distributions in the Sultanate of Oman. It also presents the 
movement of money and credit and their distributions by 
sector and governorate, as well as traffic of trading shares 
and bonds, and insurance companies operating in the 
Sultanate of Oman.

ุงุงูุฑูุงู ุงูููุงุณูุฉ ูุงูุณุนุงุฑ
Price Index

--- Page 291 ---

Introduction:
This section deals with Consumer Price Index (CPI) in the 
Sultanate of Oman - according to the different commodity 
categories - and Producer Price Index (PPI) according to 
the various economic activities.

The modified Laspeyre coefficient is the aggregate price 
index weighted by the base year quantities, was used to 
calculate both CPI and PPI in the Sultanate.
.ุงููุฑุฌุญ ูุงูุณุนุงุฑ ุจูููุงุช ุณูุฉ ุงุงูุณุงุณ
The base year of CPI was updated to be 2018 instead of 
2012 previously approved while the base year of PPI is 
also 2018 instead of 2007.

 ุุณูุทูุฉ ุนูุงู ูุดูุช ุงุฑุจุน ูุทุงุนุงุช ุงูุชุงุฌูุฉ: ูุทุงุน ุงูุตูุงุนุฉ ุงูุชุญููููุฉ
.ูุทุงุน ุงูุชุนุฏูู ูุงุณุชุบุงูู ุงููุญุงุฌุฑุ ูุทุงุน ุงูููุฑุจุงุกุ ููุทุงุน ูุงููุงุก
The prices of goods and services for CPI are collected on 
a monthly and quarterly basis automatically for a sample 
of commercial enterprises and leased housing units. The 
price collection process covers 56,640 items from 3,907 
commercial establishments and 1,509 rented residential 
units from all governorates of the Sultanate of Oman. As 
for PPI, the prices - related to four productive sectors: 
manufacturing, mining and quarrying, electricity and 
water- are collected on quarterly basis using a selected 
sample of the various governorates.
Data Sources:
- National Centre for Statistics and Information.

0.6% was the annual inflation rate in the Sultanate of

Introduction:
This section presents a set of media service indicators
in the Sultanate of Oman, such as radio and television
broadcasting hours and local newspapers and magazines
according to their periodical issuing. It also deals with a
set of culture indicators such as the numbers and types
